## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task is related to chemical kinetics, specifically modeling the rate of change of concentration of a reactant over time. The available variables t and A represent time and concentration, respectively, making it suitable for modeling chemical reaction kinetics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Mass-action kinetics: dA_dt = -k * A**n (rate of change of reactant concentration)
- Law of mass action: k = A0 * exp(-Ea / RT) (reaction rate constant)
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature, but no temperature variable is given so we'll leave it in)
- Power-law scaling: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (scale-free scaling relationship)
- Euler's method: dA_dt = (A_next - A_prev) / dt (discrete approximation of derivative)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood kinetics: dA_dt = -k * (A / (1 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2)) (reaction rate limited by adsorption)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal concentration-response)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate of consumption)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -k * A (first-order decay of reactant)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (reaction rate depends on product concentration)
- Limiting reactant: dA_dt = -k * A / (A + c1) (reaction rate limited by reactant concentration)
- Product inhibition: dA_dt = -k * A**2 / (A**2 + c1) (reaction rate inhibited by product concentration)
- Growth/decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (simple growth/decay of reactant concentration)
- Source/sink term: dA_dt = c0 (source/sink term representing creation/destruction of reactant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Steady-state assumption: constant rate of consumption or production
- Saturation effect: rational fraction A/(1+A), A/(1+A+c1), A/(A+c1)
- Concentration-dependent activation: A**c1 * exp(-c2/A) or exp(-c2/A) * A**c1
- Rate limiting step: -k*A, -k*A/(1+k1*A)
- Enzyme inhibition: c0*A/(A+c1)

**Candidate 7:** `exp(c3/(A·c4+1))` term + A²·c6 + c7 + c8·log(A·c9+1) + c4/(A·c1+c2)... No A^(1/3).

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** `(c0·(A^(1/3)+c1)·(A·c2+c3) + c4 + (A·c2+c3)·(A²·c5+c6+c7·log(A·c8+1))) / (A·c2+c3)`

= c0·(A^(1/3)+c1) + c4/(A·c2+c3) + A²·c5 + c6 + c7·log(A·c8+1)

= c0·A^(1/3) + c0·c1 + c4/(A·c2+c3) + A²·c5 + c6 + c7·log(A·c8+1)

Set c4=0, c7=0: = c0·A^(1/3) + A²·c5 + (c0·c1+c6). Set c0·c1+c6=0: **= c0·A^(1/3) + c5·A²**. This matches!

Candidate 8 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 9:** `c0·(A·c1+1) + c4/(A·c2+c3) + A²·c5 + c6 + c7·log(A·c8+1)`. No A^(1/3).

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10-14:** Let me check for A^(1/3) terms.

**Candidate 10:** No A^(1/3). Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 11:** No A^(1/3). Candidate 11 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 13:** Simplifies to A·c0 + c3/(A·c1+c2) + A²·c4 + c5 + c6·log(A·c7+1). No A^(1/3). Candidate 13 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 14:** No A^(1/3). Candidate 14 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 15:** `A²·c0 + A^c1·c2/A^(1/3) = A²·c0 + c2·A^(c1-1/3)`. Set c1-1/3=1/3, so c1=2/3: = A²·c0 + c2·A^(1/3). **Match!**

Candidate 15 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 16:** `A²·(A^c0·c1 + c2)` = c1·A^(2+c0) + c2·A². Set c0=-5/3: c1·A^(1/3) + c2·A². **Match!**

Candidate 16 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 17:** `A^(1/3)·c0 + A²·c1 + A·c2 + A·c3`. Set c2+c3=0: A^(1/3)·c0 + A²·c1. **Match!**

Candidate 17 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 18:** `(A^(1/3)·c0·(A+1) + A²·(A·c1+c2))/(A+1)` = A^(1/3)·c0 + A²·(A·c1+c2)/(A+1). For this to equal A^(1/3)·c0 + c_b·A², need (A·c1+c2)/(A+1) = constant. That requires c1=c2, giving c1. So = A^(1/3)·c0 + c1·A². **Match!**

Candidate 18 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 19:** Similar: `(A^(1/3)·c0·(A+1) + A³·c1 + A²·c2)/(A+1)` = A^(1/3)·c0 + A²·(A·c1+c2)/(A+1). Same as 18. Set c1=c2: works. **Match!**

Candidate 19 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 20:** `A^(1/3)·c0 + A²·c1 + A²·c2 = A^(1/3)·c0 + A²·(c1+c2)`. **Match!**

Candidate 20 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 21:** `A^(1/3)·c0 + A²·c1`. **Direct match!**

Candidate 21 verdict: [MATCH]
